The Science of Jadal vs the Science of Adab al-Bahth: Scope and Application
Author distinguishes the science of jadal from the science of adab al-bahth using authorities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate the science of jadal from the science of adab al-bahth wa al-munazarah by identifying their scopes and the authorities cited (Hajji Khalifah, Ibn Khaldun).

Core Idea
The science of adab al-bahth is the broader field covering all shar'i sciences, while jadal is specialized for usul al-fiqh.

Beyond the terminological distinction, the author examines the two sciences. Drawing on Hajji Khalifah and Ibn Khaldun, he shows that the science of adab al-bahth (etiquette of research and debate) is more general than the science of jadal, which is confined to usul al-fiqh. This lesson unpacks that hierarchy and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Extract Hajji Khalifah's definition
Identify the quote: 'علم آداب البحث... هو علم يبحث فيه عن كيفية إيراد الكلام بين المتناظرين'. Note that its subject is evidence and its goal is acquiring a faculty of debate.
This definition encompasses all debates.
2
Understand the author's inference
The author concludes that adab al-bahth is more general (أعم) because it applies to all shar'i sciences, while jadal is specific to usul al-fiqh. Find the sentence: 'ومعنى هذا أن علم آداب البحث والمناظرة أعم من علم الجدل'.
3
Analyze Ibn Khaldun's statement
Ibn Khaldun explains reasons for needing rules of debate. He says they preserve or demolish an opinion, whether in fiqh or other disciplines. This confirms the broader scope of adab al-bahth.
Look for 'كان ذلك الرأي من الفقه أو غيره'.
4
Synthesize the hierarchy
Combine the statements: adab al-bahth is the overarching science; jadal is a specialized branch. Hajji Khalifah even says 'الجدل أخص منه' (jadal is more specific).

Definition and Purpose of 'Ilm al-Khilaf
Author defines the purpose of 'ilm al-khilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four purposes of 'ilm al-khilaf as outlined by the author.

Core Idea
Ilm al-khilaf defends your school and attacks the opponent's.

In this passage, the author defines the science of disagreement ('ilm al-khilaf) not by its subject matter alone, but by its objectives. Understanding these purposes is essential for anyone engaging in madhhab-based juristic debate. This lesson will help you recognize the dual defensive-offensive character of 'ilm al-khilaf.

Guided Path
1
Find the definiendum and the main verb
Locate 'علم الخلاف' and the verb 'يهدف' (aims). This signals a teleological definition—defining by purpose rather than genus and differentia.
The passage does not give a strict hadd definition.
2
Extract the first two purposes: supporting and explaining
The passage mentions 'تأييد المذاهب بإيراد الحجج' (supporting schools by presenting arguments) and 'بيان القواعد والأصول' (explaining the rules and principles). These are internal strengthening functions.
3
Extract the last two purposes: repelling and refuting
The passage mentions 'دفع الشكوك' (repelling doubts) and 'رد الشبه... وإيقاعها على المذهب المخالف' (refuting ambiguities and turning them against the opponent). These are external defensive and offensive functions.
4
Synthesize the overall aim
Combine all four purposes: 'ilm al-khilaf is about both defending one's school with evidence and attacking the opposing school by rebutting its arguments.
This mirrors the dialectical method of jadal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فعلم الخلاف يهدف إلى تأييد المذاهب بإيراد الحجج والبراهين والأدلة لأقوالهم، وبيان القواعد والأصول التي اعتمدوا عليها في الاجتهاد والاستنباط، ودفع الشكوك التي ترد على المذهب، ورد الشبه التي تثار عليه، وإيقاعها على المذهب المخالف
Thus the science of disagreement aims to support the schools by presenting arguments, proofs, and evidences for their statements, and to explain the rules and principles upon which they relied in ijtihad and derivation, and to repel doubts that occur against the school, and to refute ambiguities raised against it, and to turn them against the opposing school.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage defines the purpose and scope of 'ilm al-khilaf (the science of disagreement). It outlines its objectives: supporting one's own school with evidence, clarifying the methodological foundations, defending against criticisms, and counter-attacking the opposing school. This is a definitional passage. The author lists four key functions: (1) presenting arguments and proofs for the school's positions, (2) explaining the rules and principles used in ijtihad, (3) repelling doubts against the school, and (4) refuting ambiguities and turning them against the opposing school. This mirrors the dialectical method of jadal, where arguments are both defensive and offensive.

Critiquing Ibn Khaldun's History of Jadal and Khilaf
Author presents and critiques Ibn Khaldun's historical analysis of jadal and khilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify weaknesses in Ibn Khaldun's historical analysis of the emergence of jadal and khilaf, and compare it with alternative evidence.

Core Idea
Historical narratives about Islamic sciences must be critically examined, not blindly accepted.

Ibn Khaldun's Muqaddima offers a grand narrative of Islamic history, including the development of jadal and khilaf. But his account contains biases and factual gaps. In this lesson, we will dissect his claims and see how later scholars like Dr. Muhammad al-Zuhayli refine them. You will learn to approach historical claims with analytical rigor.

Guided Path
1
Extract Ibn Khaldun's key claims
List the main points: (a) khilaf emerged after ijtihad closed and the four schools were established; (b) disagreements occur between founders; (c) Hanafis/Shafi'is wrote more because they use qiyas; (d) Malikis rely on athar and are less analytic; (e) technical writing began in the 3rd century AH.
2
Identify the author's objections
The author criticizes: exclusion of Hanbalis without justification; unsupported distinction between schools; vague dating; reliance on rational deductions over deep study.
3
Compare with alternative evidence
Dr. al-Zuhayli dates khilaf writings to the 2nd century AH, giving specific examples (Abu Hanifa vs Ibn Abi Layla, al-Shafi'i with Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, etc.).
4
Evaluate the critique's validity
Does the author provide sufficient evidence to refute Ibn Khaldun? The author points out gaps but also makes his own assumptions. Assess the strength of the critique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويحلل ابن خلدون الظروف التاريخية والثقافية العامة التي نشأ في ظلها هذا العلم وتطور، فيقول : كان للمقلدين أن يقلدوا من شاءوا منهم – أي المجتهدين لما انتهى ذلك إلى الأئمة الأربعة من علماء الأمصار، وكانوا بمكان من الظن بهم، اقتصر الناس على تقليدهم ومنعوا من تقليد سواهم لذهاب الاجتهاد وصعوبته وتشعب العلوم التي هي مواده باتصال الزمان، وافتقاد من يقوم على سوى هذه المذاهب الأربعة فأقيمت هذه المذاهب الأربعة على أصول حسن الملة. وهكذا أجريت في مسائل الشريعة كلها، وفي كل باب من أبواب الفقه، فتارة يكون الخلاف بين الشافعي ومالك، وأبو حنيفة يوافق أحدهما، وتارة بين مالك وأبي حنيفة والشافعي يوافق أحدهما، وتارة بين الشافعي وأبي حنيفة ومالك يوافق أحدهما. ومن هنا نجد ابن خلدون - الذي يعتمد بلا شك على استنباطات عقلية، أكثر من اعتماده على دراسة متعمقة في وقائع الأشياء نجده بعد أن استبعد الحنابلة، وهو خطأ فيما نظن يصل إلى إثبات تفرقة غير مدعمة، فيما يبدو لنا، بين مؤلفي المذاهب الأخرى، حيث يقول : وتأليف الحنفية والشافعية فيه أكثر تأليف المالكية، لأن القياس عند الحنفية أصل للكثير من فروع مذهبهم، كما عرفت، فهم أهل لهذا النظر والبحث، وأما المالكية فالأثر أكثر معتمدهم، وليسوا بأهل نظر، وأيضًا فأكثر أهل المغرب، وهم بادية غفل من الصنائع إلا في الأقل. ومع أن ابن خلدون يؤكد أن الخلافيات قد ظهرت على المستوى العملي، بدءًا من العصر الذي كانت المذاهب الأربعة فيه قد بدأت تفرض نفسها بخاصة على الأمة الإسلامية، أعني منذ القرن الثالث الهجري التاسع الميلادي، فإنه لا يحدد هذه الفترة - التي بدأت فيها الكتابة في هذا النوع، بطريقة فنية ومنهجية. في حين يرى الدكتور محمد الزحيلي أن المؤلفات في علم الخلاف بدأت تظهر منذ القرن الثاني الهجري، كاختلاف أبي حنيفة وابن أبي ليلى، والرد على الأوزاعي، واختلاف الشافعي مع محمد بن الحسن، واختلاف الشافعي مع مالك، وغيرها
And Ibn Khaldun analyzes the general historical and cultural circumstances in which this science emerged and developed, so he says: The muqallids could imitate whomever they wished among the mujtahids, until that came to the four Imams from the scholars of the major cities, and they were in a position of trust, so the people limited themselves to imitating them and prevented imitating others because ijtihad had disappeared, its difficulty, the branching of the sciences that are its materials due to the passage of time, and the lack of anyone who could follow other than these four schools, so these four schools were established upon sound foundations of the religion. Thus it was carried out in all matters of Sharia, and in every chapter of jurisprudence, so sometimes the disagreement is between al-Shafi'i and Malik, and Abu Hanifa agrees with one of them, and sometimes between Malik and Abu Hanifa, and al-Shafi'i agrees with one of them, and sometimes between al-Shafi'i and Abu Hanifa, and Malik agrees with one of them. And from here we find Ibn Khaldun - who no doubt relies on rational deductions more than on deep study of the facts of things - we find him after having excluded the Hanbalis, which is in our opinion an error that reaches the point of establishing an unsupported distinction, as it appears to us, between the authors of the other schools, where he says: The writings of the Hanafis and Shafi'is in this field are more than the writings of the Malikis, because analogy (qiyas) for the Hanafis is a source for many branches of their school, as you know, so they are people of this contemplation and research, while the Malikis rely more on tradition (athar), and they are not people of contemplation, and also most of the people of the Maghreb are Bedouin ignorant of the sciences except in the rare case. And although Ibn Khaldun confirms that the scholastic disagreements appeared on the practical level, starting from the era in which the four schools began to impose themselves especially on the Islamic nation, meaning from the third century AH/ninth century CE, he does not specify this period - in which writing in this genre began in a technical and methodological manner. While Dr. Muhammad al-Zuhayli holds that writings in the science of disagreement began to appear from the second century AH, such as the disagreement of Abu Hanifa and Ibn Abi Layla, and the refutation of al-Awza'i, and the disagreement of al-Shafi'i with Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, and the disagreement of al-Shafi'i with Malik, and others.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage presents Ibn Khaldun's historical analysis of the emergence of jadal and 'ilm al-khilaf, followed by a critical evaluation by the author. Ibn Khaldun ties the development to the period after ijtihad declined and the four schools became established. He describes how disagreement occurs between the founders and their followers. The author then critiques Ibn Khaldun for excluding the Hanbalis and for making an unsupported distinction between the Hanafis/Shafi'is (who relied more on qiyas) and the Malikis (who relied more on athar). The author also notes Ibn Khaldun's vagueness about the exact period when technical writing began. Finally, the author cites Dr. Muhammad al-Zuhayli, who places the beginning of such writings in the second century AH, earlier than Ibn Khaldun's third century, and gives examples. The passage is critical in nature, as the author challenges Ibn Khaldun's claims and offers alternative evidence.

Distinguishing Ilm al-Khilaf from Ilm al-Jadal
Author distinguishes 'ilm al-khilaf from 'ilm al-jadal by subject matter and methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between 'ilm al-khilaf and 'ilm al-jadal based on their subject matter and methodology, and correctly classify examples of issues into each category.

Core Idea
Khilaf studies furu' (branches); jadal studies usul (foundations) – both use the same methods.

In the Islamic intellectual tradition, two disciplines – 'ilm al-khilaf and 'ilm al-jadal – often appear together but serve different purposes. This passage clarifies the distinction between them, showing that while they share methodology, their scope differs: khilaf covers differences on furu' (specific rulings), while jadal focuses on usul (foundational principles). Understanding this distinction is crucial for navigating juristic debates and analyzing arguments correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sciences
Read the passage and note the two disciplines being compared: 'ilm al-khilaf and 'ilm al-jadal. Recognize that the author states the difference is only in the subject matter (al-madda).
2
Extract subject matter difference
Find where the author says khilaf relates to furu' al-fiqh and jadal touches usul al-fiqh. Write down the contrast: furu' vs usul.
3
List topics under jadal
The author enumerates several topics covered in jadal: interpretation of Qur'an (general/specific, command/prohibition, abrogation), hadith criticism, consensus, analogy, and other principles like istihsan, istishab, istislah. List these as foundational issues (usul).
4
List topics under khilaf
The author mentions that khilaf goes through chapters of fiqh: prayer, zakat, fasting, etc. Recognize that these are specific rulings (furu').
5
Note methodological similarity
The author explicitly states that in terms of methodology, the two sciences do not differ; they use the same proofs and methods of disputation. This is an important nuance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الثاني : الفرق بين علم الخلاف وعلم الجدل مسألة والفرق بين علم الخلاف وعلم الجدل إنما هو في المادة المدروسة في كل منهما فحسب، إذ الخلافيات تتعلق بفروع الفقه، بينما يمس الجدل أصوله، فالمؤلف في باب الجدل يأتي على مسائل الخلاف الأصولية مسألة بعد ويسوق كل الآراء التي صدرت حول كل واحدة منها، وذلك حرصا منه على نقض الآراء المخالفة لمذهبه أو حتى التي تخالف رأيه الخاص إن كان من المجتهدين داخل المذهب فإذا كان المؤلف في باب الخلافيات يعالج المسائل المختلف فيها في كل باب أبواب الفقه في باب الصلاة، ثم الزكاة، ثم الصيام، ثم الحج، ثم الأيمان والنذور، وهكذا إلى آخر أبواب الفقه .. فإن المؤلف في باب الجدل في أصول الفقه يخوض في قضايا تأويل القرآن ويبحث في المنهجية القرآنية القائمة على معاني العموم والخصوص، والأمر والنهي، والناسخ والمنسوخ، وفي ما يرجع إلى كل صنف من هذه المصطلحات، وإذا ما وصل إلى الحديث اعتمد هذه القضايا بالذات ولكن مضيفا إليها ما تعلق منها خاصة بمنهجية نقده التاريخي، الداخلي والخارجي، من التأمل في طرق نقله وإثبات صحته، وينتهي إلى الإجماع فينظر في حجيته الشرعية إثباتا أو نفيا وفي طريقة تصوره وإمكانية ذلك عقليا ونقليا، وأخيرًا في كيفية انعقاده وما تستوجب من شروط، من حيث انقراض العصر من جهة وكفاءة المجتهدين من جهة أخرى، حتى إذا ما وصل إلى القياس خاض في حجيته لإثباتها أو نفيها اعتمادًا على النقل من القرآن والحديث والإجماع، والعقل أيضًا؛ ولا يفوته البحث في أصول أخرى تلحق بهذه الأربعة السابقة وتتبعها في الأهمية كالاستحسان والاستصحاب والاستصلاح وغيرها ولعل هذا المعنى هو ما أراده محمد صدیق حسن خان حين أرجع الفرق بين علم الجدل من جهة وعلم الخلاف من جهة ثانية إلى أن البحث في الجدل بحسب المادة، وفي الخلاف بحسب الصورة هذا فيما يتعلق بالفرق بين العلمين من حيث الموضوع، أما من حيث المنهج فهما لا يختلفان باعتبارهما ينبعان من مشكاة واحدة وقد دعت إلى نشأتهما وتطورهما أسباب مشتركة فهما يستخدمان نفس الأدلة، ويسيران عبر طرق واحدة في المناظرة والحجاج.
The Second Topic: The Difference Between the Science of Disagreement (Khilaf) and the Science of Dialectic (Jadal). Question: The difference between the science of khilaf and the science of jadal is only in the subject matter studied in each of them. For the issues of khilaf relate to the branches of fiqh, while jadal touches its foundations. The author, in the section on jadal, addresses the foundational issues of khilaf one by one and cites all the opinions that have been issued concerning each one, out of his eagerness to refute the opinions opposing his school or even those that oppose his own view if he is among the mujtahids within the school. For if the author, in the section on khilafiyat, deals with the issues that are differed upon in each chapter of the chapters of fiqh—in the chapter of prayer, then zakat, then fasting, then pilgrimage, then oaths and vows, and so on to the end of the chapters of fiqh—then the author, in the section on jadal in usul al-fiqh, plunges into issues of interpretation of the Qur'an and investigates the Qur'anic methodology based on the meanings of generality and specificity, command and prohibition, abrogating and abrogated, and what pertains to each category of these terms. And when he reaches the hadith, he adopts these very issues but adds to them what relates specifically to the methodology of its historical criticism, internal and external, from examining the methods of its transmission and establishing its authenticity. And he ends with consensus, examining its legal authority positively or negatively, and the method of its conception and the possibility of that rationally and textually, and finally how it is established and the conditions it requires, in terms of the extinction of the era on one hand, and the competence of the mujtahids on the other hand. Until when he reaches analogy, he plunges into its authority to prove or negate it, relying on transmission from the Qur'an, hadith, consensus, and reason as well. And he does not neglect research into other foundations that attach to these four preceding ones and follow them in importance, such as istihsan, istishab, istislah, and others. And perhaps this meaning is what Muhammad Siddiq Hasan Khan intended when he attributed the difference between the science of jadal on one hand and the science of khilaf on the other to the fact that research in jadal is in terms of material, and in khilaf in terms of form. This is concerning the difference between the two sciences in terms of subject matter. As for methodology, they do not differ, because they emanate from the same niche and common causes called for their emergence and development. They use the same proofs and follow the same paths in disputation and argumentation.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage defines and distinguishes between two related sciences: 'ilm al-khilaf and 'ilm al-jadal. The author begins by stating that the difference is solely in the subject matter (al-madda). Khilaf deals with the branches (furu') of fiqh, while jadal deals with the foundations (usul). He then elaborates by contrasting the approaches of a typical khilaf author and a jadal author. The khilaf author goes through each chapter of fiqh (prayer, zakat, etc.) and presents the differences of opinion. The jadal author, by contrast, works through foundational issues: interpretation of the Qur'an (including general/specific, command/prohibition, abrogation), hadith criticism, consensus (its authority and conditions), and analogy (qiyas), as well as other principles like istihsan, istishab, and istislah. He then cites Muhammad Siddiq Hasan Khan to summarize that jadal is about the material and khilaf about the form. Finally, he notes that in terms of methodology, the two sciences are the same: they use the same proofs and methods of disputation. All examples here are from usul al-fiqh and fiqh disciplines, consistent with the Islamic sciences focus.

Key Terms
علم الخلاف
علم الجدل
المادة
الصورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Ilm al-khilaf and ilm al-jadal are distinguished by subject matter (furu' vs usul) but share methodology, both using the same proofs and methods of disputation.

The Definition and Importance of Rational Consideration in Usuli Dialectic
Author defines rational consideration (nazar 'aqli) and explains its foundational role in usuli dialectic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define rational consideration (al-nazar al-'aqli) and explain its foundational role in usuli dialectic (al-jadal al-usuli).

Core Idea
Rational consideration is the firm pillar of usuli dialectic; without it, no valid debate can occur.

This passage from our jadal usuli text defines rational consideration and argues that it is the essential foundation of all dialectical reasoning in usul al-fiqh. The author distinguishes general Shari'a reasoning from its specific application in usul, then demonstrates why jadal collapses without it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contexts of nazar
Notice how the author first defines rational consideration in a general Shari'a context (conditions of ijtihad, rules, methods) and then narrows it to usul al-fiqh (investigation of evidences to derive and verify usul rules).
2
Extract the components of nazar in usul
From the definition: nazar in usul involves deriving rules, verifying them, repelling refutations, clarifying boundaries, and defining the scope of each rule.
3
Explain the dependency of jadal on nazar
The author states that all ideas and opinions in usuli dialectic are derived through rational consideration. Without it, the dialectic cannot be established. Nazar is the foundation for forming one's own opinion, evaluating the opponent's view, and constructing proofs.
4
Summarize the logical role of nazar
Rational consideration is not merely a tool but the essential support (rukn rakīn) for every stage of dialectical engagement. It underlies both the substance and the procedure of jadal.

ج - النظر العقلي : بعد هذا يمكن أن نقول بأن النظر العقلي الذي نريده في هذا البحث هو : تأمل الإنسان وتفكره بعقله في علوم الشرع، من جهة النظر في شروط الاجتهاد وقواعده وسبل الاجتهاد ومسالكه ونتائجه . أما النظر العقلي في أصول الفقه، فنعني به البحث الفكري والتأمل العقلي في الأدلة لاستخلاص القواعد الأصولية، وتحقيقها، ودفع ما قد ينقضها، وبيان حدودها، ومجال عمل كل منها . المطلب الثاني : أهمية النظر العقلي في الجدل الأصولي الجدل الأصولي هو عبارة عن حوار أفكار وآراء في المسائل الأصولية، والأفكار والآراء مهما كانت إنما يتم استمدادها بواسطة النظر العقلي، لذلك كان للنظر العقلي أهمية خاصة في الجدل الأصولي، إذ يعتبر الركن الركين في هذا الجدل فلا يمكن أن يقوم جدل دون أن يرتكز في مجرياته ومعطياته على النظر العقلي. فالنظر العقلي هو الأساس فيما يقرره كل واحد من طرفي الجدل من رأي في المسألة أولاً، وهو الأساس فيما ينظر به إلى رأي المخالف، وهو المرتكز فيما يبني عليه استدلاله وحججه على ما يذهب إليه، وكذلك هو المستند في
C - Rational Consideration (al-Nazar al-'Aqli): After this we can say that rational consideration as we intend it in this research is: man's contemplation and thinking with his intellect in the sciences of the Shari'a, from the perspective of examining the conditions of ijtihad, its rules, methods, pathways, and results. As for rational consideration in usul al-fiqh, we mean by it: intellectual investigation and rational contemplation of the evidences to derive the usul rules, to verify them, to repel what may refute them, to clarify their boundaries, and the scope of operation of each. The Second Section: The Importance of Rational Consideration in Usuli Dialectic. Usuli dialectic (al-jadal al-usuli) is a dialogue of ideas and opinions in usul issues, and ideas and opinions, whatever they may be, are only derived through rational consideration. Therefore, rational consideration has special importance in usuli dialectic, for it is considered the firm pillar in this dialectic. No dialectic can be established without being based, in its proceedings and data, on rational consideration. Rational consideration is the foundation of what each of the two parties of the dialectic decides in opinion on the issue first, and it is the foundation for how one looks at the opponent's opinion, and it is the basis upon which one builds his inference and proofs for what he holds, and likewise it is the support in...
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage defines al-nazar al-'aqli (rational consideration) and explains its central importance in jadal usuli (usuli dialectic). The author first gives a general definition: nazar 'aqli is man's contemplation and thinking with his intellect regarding the sciences of the Shari'a, encompassing the examination of ijtihad conditions, rules, methods, pathways, and results. He then specifies the meaning in usul al-fiqh: intellectual investigation and rational contemplation of the evidences (adilla) to derive usul rules, verify them, refute objections, and clarify boundaries and scope. The author then turns to the importance of this type of reasoning in usuli dialectic, which is defined as a dialogue of ideas and opinions in usul issues. He argues that all ideas and opinions are derived through rational consideration, so nazar 'aqli is the firm pillar (al-rukn al-rakīn) of this dialectic. Without it, no dialectic can proceed, because everything—forming one's own opinion, evaluating the opponent's view, constructing arguments and proofs—depends on rational consideration. The passage thus establishes that rational consideration is not merely one component but the essential foundation of all dialectical engagement in usul al-fiqh.

Rational Consideration as the Foundation of Jadal Usuli
Author defines jadal usuli and explains nazar's indispensable roles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four key roles of nazar 'aqli in usul dialectic as described by the author.

Core Idea
Jadal without nazar is blind; nazar is the pillar that supports every stage of dialectical exchange.

In this passage, the author establishes that usul dialectic (jadal usuli) is entirely dependent on rational consideration (nazar 'aqli). He details four specific functions that nazar plays: forming one's own opinion, evaluating the opponent's view, building arguments, and mounting objections. He also notes that this reliance is why jadal is often called munazara, an exchange of consideration. Let's unpack these roles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of jadal usuli
Find the author's definition: it is a dialogue of ideas in usul issues. Note that it is based on nazar.
2
Locate the four roles of nazar
The author lists four foundations: (1) deciding one's own opinion, (2) looking at the opponent's opinion, (3) building reasoning and arguments, (4) objections against the opponent's evidence. Extract each from the Arabic.
These are the practical functions of nazar in dialectical exchange.
3
Understand the connection to munazara
The author quotes al-Shirazi saying that councils of nazar are councils of jadal. Why? Because jadal occurs through thought and consideration (nazar).
This shows the terminological overlap.
4
Reflect on the necessity
The author states that dialectic cannot occur without being based on nazar. Consider why: without rational consideration, dialectic would be mere assertion.
This underscores nazar's epistemological primacy.

المطلب الثاني : أهمية النظر العقلي في الجدل الأصولي الجدل الأصولي هو عبارة عن حوار أفكار وآراء في المسائل الأصولية، والأفكار والآراء مهما كانت إنما يتم استمدادها بواسطة النظر العقلي، لذلك كان للنظر العقلي أهمية خاصة في الجدل الأصولي، إذ يعتبر الركن الركين في هذا الجدل فلا يمكن أن يقوم جدل دون أن يرتكز في مجرياته ومعطياته على النظر العقلي. فالنظر العقلي هو الأساس فيما يقرره كل واحد من طرفي الجدل من رأي في المسألة أولاً ، وهو الأساس فيما ينظر به إلى رأي المخالف، وهو المرتكز فيما يبني عليه استدلاله وحججه على ما يذهب إليه، وكذلك هو المستند في اعتراضاته على أدلة المخالف، إذ يكد عقله ويعمل ذهنه في محاولة الوقوف على جوانب الضعف في أدلة المخالف ويحاول من خلال ذلك هدمها وإسقاط الاستدلال بها. لذلك كان الجدل يسمى في الكثير من الأحيان مناظرة، لأنه تبادل للنظر بين طرفي الجدل، قال الشيرازي: وسميت مجالس النظر بذلك، وإن كانت في الحقيقة مجالس الجدل، لأن الجدل الواقع فيها يقع عن الفكر والنظر»(1) وفي بيان أهمية النظر العقلي ووجه الحاجة إليه في دراسة الشريعة بوجه عام، يقول الإمام جمال الدين القاسمي رحمه الله : «النظر قانون الاستدلال في الأمور، وحاكم العدل، وقاضي الصدق، وبرهان الشريعة، ومحك الحق والباطل وبريد المعرفة وسلطان الحقيقة، وترجمان الإيمان، وحجة الأنبياء، ومحجة الأولياء، والسيف القاطع على الأعداء، شجرة طيبة أصلها ثابت وفرعها في السماء، فالنظر رأس السعادة عند أهل الدنيا والدين. فأساس التدبير وصحة الاعتقاد وخلاصة التوحيد في ناصية النظر، كما أن أساس الكفر والشرك في جانب التقليد. فإن قيل : ما الحجة على صحة النظر وأنه مؤد إلى العلم(3)؟ فيقال : إن في العلم حقا وباطلا والناس صنفان : أهل الحق وأهل الباطل، ولا يتصور معرفة الحق من الباطل إلا بالنظر، والإنسان خلق كامل الرأي عظيم الفكر دراكا للمعاني، وأتي الإدراك وهو العقل، فإذا استعمله على وجهه وقع عنده العلم بالمنظور فيه، كما يقع العلم بالمدركات عند الإدراك، فعند فتح الأجفان يبصر
Second topic: The importance of rational consideration in usul dialectic. Usul dialectic is a dialogue of ideas and opinions in usul issues, and ideas and opinions, whatever they are, are only derived by means of rational consideration. Therefore, rational consideration has special importance in usul dialectic, for it is considered the firm pillar in this dialectic. Dialectic cannot occur without being based in its proceedings and data on rational consideration. Rational consideration is the foundation of what each of the two sides of the dialectic decides in opinion on the issue first, and it is the foundation of what he looks at of the opponent's opinion, and it is the basis on which he builds his reasoning and arguments for what he advocates, and likewise it is the reliance in his objections to the opponent's evidence, as he strains his intellect and works his mind in attempting to identify weaknesses in the opponent's evidence and through that tries to demolish them and invalidate the argument with them. Therefore, dialectic was often called 'munazara', because it is an exchange of consideration between the two sides of dialectic. Al-Shirazi said: 'The councils of consideration were named thus, even though they are in reality councils of dialectic, because the dialectic occurring in them occurs through thought and consideration.' (1) And in explaining the importance of rational consideration and the need for it in studying the Law in general, Imam Jamal al-Din al-Qasimi, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'Consideration is the law of inference in matters, the just ruler, the truthful judge, the proof of the Law, the touchstone of truth and falsehood, the courier of knowledge, the sultan of reality, the interpreter of faith, the argument of the prophets, the path of the saints, and the piercing sword against enemies, a goodly tree whose root is firmly fixed and its branches in the sky. So consideration is the head of happiness for the people of this world and religion. The foundation of management, correctness of belief, and essence of monotheism lies in the forelock of consideration, just as the foundation of disbelief and polytheism lies in the side of blind imitation.' If it is said: What is the evidence for the validity of consideration and that it leads to knowledge? (3) Then it is said: Indeed, in knowledge there is truth and falsehood, and people are two categories: people of truth and people of falsehood, and it is inconceivable to know truth from falsehood except through consideration. And man was created complete in opinion, great in thought, perceiver of meanings, and perception was given, which is the intellect. So if he uses it in its proper way, knowledge of what is considered occurs to him, just as knowledge of perceptibles occurs upon perception. So when the eyelids are opened, he sees.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage explains why rational consideration (nazar 'aqli) is crucial in usul dialectic (jadal usuli). The author first states that jadal usuli is a dialogue fully dependent on nazar for its ideas. Nazar is the foundation for each side's opinion, examination of the opponent's view, construction of arguments, and objections against the opponent. Because it involves exchange of nazar, jadal is often called munazara. The author then quotes al-Shirazi confirming that councils of nazar are councils of jadal. Next, a quote from al-Qasimi praises nazar as the law of inference, the touchstone of truth, etc., contrasting it with taqlid which leads to disbelief. Finally, a proof of nazar's validity is presented: (1) knowledge contains truth and falsehood; (2) people are divided into truth-seekers and falsehood-followers; (3) distinguishing truth from falsehood only occurs through nazar; (4) man is endowed with intellect; (5) using intellect correctly yields knowledge of what is considered, just as opening eyes yields sight. Therefore, nazar leads to knowledge.

Key Terms
الجدل الأصولي
النظر العقلي
المناظرة

Key Takeaway

The Proof for the Validity of Rational Consideration
Al-Qasimi defends nazar's validity with a multi-premise argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the compound argument that al-Qasimi uses to prove that nazar 'aqli leads to certain knowledge.

Core Idea
Nazar is the eye of the mind; just as the eye sees when opened, the intellect knows when it considers.

After establishing the importance of nazar, the author addresses a potential objection: what is the proof that nazar is valid and leads to knowledge? He presents a multi-part argument that appeals to the nature of knowledge, the division of people, and the endowment of intellect. This argument is a compound inference that combines several premises to reach a conclusion. In this lesson, we will break it down into its logical components.

Guided Path
1
Identify the question being answered
The passage begins with 'If it is said: What is the evidence...?' Find the question and note its challenge.
The question is: 'What is the evidence for the validity of consideration and that it leads to knowledge?'
2
Extract the premises of the argument
The author gives four premises: (1) In knowledge there is truth and falsehood. (2) People are of two categories: truth and falsehood. (3) Distinguishing truth from falsehood can only occur through nazar. (4) Man is created with intellect, and using it correctly produces knowledge.
These are the foundational claims.
3
Understand the analogy
The author compares using intellect to opening eyelids: when opened, one sees. So when intellect is used correctly, knowledge occurs.
This analogy strengthens the conclusion.
4
Construct the compound argument
Combine the premises: We know there is truth and falsehood. We need to distinguish them. Only nazar can do that. Man has the tool (intellect). Using it correctly yields knowledge. Therefore, nazar is valid and leads to knowledge.
This is a compound argument with multiple steps, not a simple syllogism.

Zann as a Valid Basis for Legal Rulings
Author explains that conjecture (zann) is a legitimate source of legal rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conjecture (zann) and certainty (ilm) in Islamic legal theory and explain why conjecture is a valid basis for rulings.

Core Idea
Conjecture from proper indications is binding, equal to certainty except when they conflict.

This passage tackles a foundational question in usul al-fiqh: can a mujtahid base a ruling on mere conjecture? The author defends the legitimacy of zann, citing several major jurists. As you read, you will learn how zann is like certainty in its binding force, but differs when the two conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim about zann
Find the opening statement where the author asserts that conjecture (zann) is a path to a ruling and must be acted upon. Note that it is placed on par with certain knowledge (ilm) except when they conflict.
The claim sets up the epistemological framework.
2
Compare the three scholarly quotes
Read the quotes from Abu Ya'la, al-Razi, and al-Tufi. Each clarifies why zann is binding: Abu Ya'la ties it to a proper indication (amara), al-Razi distinguishes between certainty of the obligation and certainty of the ruling, and al-Tufi grounds it in experiential certainty.
These quotes provide evidentiary support for the author's position.
3
Distinguish between certainty of obligation and certainty of ruling
Al-Razi says the mujtahid is certain of the obligation to act upon his conjecture, not certain of the ruling itself. Understand how this resolves the tension: the ruling is known with certainty as an obligation, while the conjecture lies in the path to it.
This is a key nuance in the epistemology of ijtihad.
4
Recognize the fallibility of the inquirer
The final paragraph notes that attaining certainty or conjecture is not guaranteed—the inquirer may err. This shows that the process is not automatic; it depends on correct method and evidence.
This balances the authority of conjecture with the reality of human fallibility.

وأنه طريق للظن» (1) . والظن واجب العمل به في الشريعة الإسلامية باعتباره طريقا من طرق إفادة الأحكام الشرعية، لا فرق في ذلك بينه وبين العلم الثابت بالدليل القطعي، ووجه (2) الفرق بينهما عند التعارض فحسب، حيث يقدم القطعي على الظني . قال أبو يعلى : الظن طريق للحكم إذا كان عن أمارة مقتضية للظن، ولهذا يجب العمل بخبر الواحد إذا كان ثقة ويجب العمل بشهادة الشاهدين وخبر المقومين إذا كانا عدلين ويجب العمل بالقياس وإن كانت علة القياس مظنونة وقال الرازي: المجتهد إذا غلب على ظنه مشاركة صورة لصورة في مناط الحكم، قطع بوجوب العمل بما أدى إليه ظنه ، فالحكم معلوم قطعًا، والظن واقع في طريقه (3). وقال نجم الدين الطوفي: إن الفقيه إذا غلب على ظنه أن الحكم كذا، علم قطعا بحصول ذلك الظن، لأنه أمر وجداني كالصحة والسقم واللذة والألم، يقطع الإنسان بوجود ذلك نفسه، وعلم قطعا بوجوب العمل عليه بمقتضى ذلك الظن، بناء على ما ثبت من أن الظن موجب للعمل أي : إذا غلب على ظن المجتهد حكم، وجب عليه العمل والفتيا إذا سئلها» (4) من هذا، ولابد من الإشارة في نهاية هذا المبحث إلى أن وصول الناظر إلى العلم أو الظن في المسألة المنظور فيها، ليس أمرًا ضروريًا أو حتميا، لأن الناظر «قد يصيب وقد يخطئ، وكلاهما نظر منه ، وقد ينظر في شبهة وفي دليل، وقد يصل بنظره إلى العلم تارة إذا سلك فيه المسلك الصحيح ورتبه على واجبه ومقتضاه، وقد لا يصل إليه إذا قصر وغلط وخلط فيه، أو نظر فيما هو شبهة وليس بدليل (5)
And that it is a path to conjecture. Conjecture must be acted upon in Islamic law as it is a means of deriving legal rulings; there is no difference in this between it and knowledge established by decisive proof. The only difference between them is when they conflict, where the decisive is given precedence over the conjectural. Abu Ya'la said: Conjecture is a path to a ruling if it arises from an indication that necessitates conjecture; for this reason, one must act upon the report of a single trustworthy narrator, the testimony of two just witnesses, the report of valuators if they are just, and analogical reasoning even if its cause is conjectural. Al-Razi said: When conjecture predominates for the mujtahid that one case shares the ratio legis with another, he is certain of the obligation to act upon what his conjecture has led to, so the ruling is known with certainty, and the conjecture lies in its path. Najm al-Din al-Tufi said: When the jurist's conjecture predominates that the ruling is such-and-such, he is certain of the occurrence of that conjecture, because it is an experiential matter like health, sickness, pleasure, and pain—a person is certain of its existence in himself—and he is certain of the obligation to act upon that conjecture, based on the established principle that conjecture necessitates action, i.e., if conjecture predominates for the mujtahid regarding a ruling, he must act and give fatwa if asked. From this, it must be noted at the end of this discussion that the inquirer's attainment of knowledge or conjecture regarding the matter under investigation is neither necessary nor inevitable, because the inquirer may hit or miss, and both are his inquiry; he may look into a sophism or into evidence, and he may sometimes attain knowledge through his inquiry if he follows the correct path and arranges it as required and necessitated, and he may not attain it if he falls short, errs, or confuses, or if he looks into a sophism that is not evidence.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage discusses the epistemological status of conjecture (zann) in Islamic legal theory. The author begins by stating that conjecture is a valid path to legal rulings and must be acted upon, equal in this respect to certain knowledge (ilm), except when they conflict, in which case certainty takes precedence. He then quotes three scholars to support this view. Abu Ya'la points out that conjecture arising from a proper indication necessitates action, giving examples such as the report of a single trustworthy narrator, testimony of witnesses, and analogical reasoning. Al-Razi adds that the mujtahid's certainty is about the obligation to act upon his conjecture, not about the ruling itself; the ruling is known with certainty (as an obligation), while the conjecture is in the path to it. Al-Tufi explains that the occurrence of conjecture is an internal, experiential certainty, and the obligation to act upon it is also certain based on the principle that conjecture necessitates action. Finally, the author notes that attaining certainty or conjecture is not guaranteed, as the inquirer may err or follow false evidence.

العلم
القطعي

Zann from a valid indication is binding in Islamic law, though it yields to certainty when they conflict, and the inquirer may not always attain it.

Importance of Definition in Jadal and Usul
Author explains the crucial role of terminology and definition in dialectic and usul al-fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of definition to a usul al-fiqh debate by identifying the key term that needs definition.

Core Idea
The keys to the sciences are their terminologies; definition is the first step in any dialectical inquiry.

In this passage, the author establishes that definitions (hadd or ta'rif) are not mere preliminaries but the essential foundation for any scholarly discussion, especially in dialectic (jadal) and usul al-fiqh. You will see how usul scholars always begin by defining the central term of a debate, and why this practice is crucial for clarity and progress. By understanding this, you will learn how to approach complex usul issues with the right methodological tool.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's central claim
The author states that terminologies are the keys to the sciences and their ultimate fruits. This means that grasping the precise meaning of technical terms is the gateway to understanding any discipline.
Notice the quote: 'مفاتيح العلوم مصطلحاتها'.
2
Extract the methodological rule
According to the author, usul scholars always start their study of an issue by defining the term around which the issue revolves. This shows that definition is not optional but a foundational step.
Look for the phrase 'أول مسألة يبدؤون بها'.
3
Analyze the components of a proper definition
The author mentions that a complete definition includes precise meaning, qualifiers (muhtazarat), and restrictions. These ensure the definition is comprehensive (jami') and exclusive (mani').
Think about how this connects to the logical criteria of a good definition.
4
Connect definition to dialectic
The author implies that without a clear definition, debates become confused. By establishing the meaning of the central term, disputants have a common ground, making dialectic productive.
Consider a real usul dispute: the definition of 'qiyas' is often the starting point.

المطلب الثالث : أهمية الحد أو التعريف في الجدل مفاتيح العلوم مصطلحاتها ومصطلحات العلوم ثمارها القصوى، فهي مجمع حقائقها المعرفية وعنوان ما به يتميز كل واحد منها عما سواه، وليس من مسلك يتوسل به الإنسان إلى منطق العلم غير ألفاظه الاصطلاحية»(2). لذلك تنطوي قضية المصطلح عند الأصوليين على أهمية بالغة، بل إنها تعتبر عندهم القضية الأساس في الدراسة الأصولية، فلا يكادون يتناولون قضية أصولية بالدراسة والبحث إلا وتكون أول مسألة يبدؤون بها فيها هي تحديد المصطلح الذي تدور عليه القضية كلها، وذلك ببيان المعنى الدقيق له عندهم، وذكر محترزاته والقيود التي تجعله جامعا لمواصفات موضوعه مانعا لدخول غيرها عليه - فالتعريف الاصطلاحي أو الحد كما يسميه الأصوليون - يشكل القضية الأولى التي يتناولونها بصدد دراستهم للمسائل الأصولية، وهذا لما أدركوه من أهمية لقضية المصطلح التي تصبح المحور العام للقضية المبحوثة كلها، ولا يمكن فهم القضية فهما واضحًا شاملا ، إلا بعد الإحاطة بمعنى المصطلح الذي هو المحور الجامع والكلي لها. وإذا علمنا أن مسائل أصول الفقه قد دار حولها جدل كبير بين علماء أصول
The Third Topic: The Importance of Definition (al-hadd or al-ta'rif) in Dialectic. The keys to the sciences are their terminologies, and the terminologies of the sciences are their ultimate fruits. They are the repository of their cognitive realities and the title by which each one is distinguished from others. There is no path through which one arrives at the logic of a science other than its technical terms. Therefore, the issue of terminology among the usul scholars is of immense importance; indeed, it is considered by them to be the fundamental issue in the study of usul. They hardly ever undertake the study and research of a usul issue without the first matter they begin with being the definition of the term around which the entire issue revolves. This is by clarifying its precise meaning according to them and mentioning its qualifiers (muhtazarat) and restrictions that make it comprehensive for the characteristics of its subject and preventive of anything else entering it. So, the technical definition (al-ta'rif al-istilahi) or the hadd, as the usul scholars call it, constitutes the first issue they address when studying usul matters. This is because they have realized the importance of the issue of terminology, which becomes the central axis of the entire discussed issue. The issue cannot be understood clearly and comprehensively except after grasping the meaning of the term that is the comprehensive and universal pivot for it. And if we know that the matters of usul al-fiqh have been the subject of great debate among usul scholars...
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is a methodological reflection on the role of definition (hadd or ta'rif) within the discipline of jadal (dialectic) and usul al-fiqh. The author asserts that terminologies are the keys to the sciences; they encapsulate the core realities and distinguish each science from others. Consequently, for scholars of usul al-fiqh, the issue of terminology is paramount. They invariably begin their study of any usul question by defining the central term around which the discussion revolves. This definition includes precise meaning, qualifiers (muhtazarat), and restrictions that ensure it includes all relevant instances and excludes extraneous ones. The author explains that the technical definition (al-ta'rif al-istilahi) or hadd is the first topic they address because it serves as the universal pivot for the entire issue; without a clear grasp of the term, comprehensive understanding is impossible. The passage concludes by noting that usul al-fiqh matters have been subjects of extensive debate, implying that precise definition is essential to resolving such debates. For example, disputes about whether qiyas (analogical reasoning) is a valid source of law depend on a precise definition of qiyas that distinguishes it from other forms of reasoning. Thus, definition is not a mere preliminary but the foundation of dialectical inquiry.

Key Terms
الحد (al-hadd): In this context, the technical definition that specifies the precise meaning of a term, including its qualifiers and restrictions. [Note: In logic, hadd often refers to a definition by genus and differentia; here it is used broadly for any technical definition.]
المصطلح (al-mustalah): A technical term specific to a science, whose precise meaning must be established for proper discussion.
الجدل (al-jadal): Dialectic or disputation, where definition is used to clarify positions and resolve disagreements.
أصول الفقه (usul al-fiqh): The discipline that studies the sources and methods of deriving Islamic legal rulings.

Key Takeaway

Critiquing Definitions in the Dialectical Method
Method of critiquing contradictory definitions in jadal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the steps of the dialectical method for critiquing definitions in usul al-fiqh and apply it to al-Juwayni's definition of 'bayan'.

Core Idea
Jadal defends your definition by systematically dismantling alternatives.

In the study of usul al-fiqh, defining key terms is not enough. Scholars must defend their definitions against competing views. This passage explains the third step of the dialectical method: after presenting one's own definition, one must critique other definitions to reveal their weaknesses. This process secures the correctness of the chosen definition and invalidates alternatives.

Guided Path
1
Present your definition
The usuli first offers his own definition of the term being studied.
This definition may be original or adopted from a previous scholar.
2
Identify alternative definitions
List the definitions given by other schools or scholars.
3
Analyze each alternative for defects
Examine each alternative to find logical, linguistic, or methodological flaws.
Look for inconsistencies, over-inclusiveness, under-inclusiveness, etc.
4
Refute each alternative
Present arguments that invalidate the flawed definitions.
The refutation should directly target the defect identified.
5
Conclude the correctness of your definition
After refuting alternatives, assert that your definition is sound and theirs are false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ج - نقد التعريفات المخالفة : خضوعا لمنطق المنهج الجدلي، فإن الأصولي لا يكتفي فحسب بتقديم تعريفه للمصطلح، بل ينتقل بعد ذلك إلى نقد تعريفات الاتجاهات الأخرى ويبين مواضع الخلل فيها، ثم يرد عليها بما ينقضها ويفضي إلى التأكيد على صحة مذهبه في التعريف وبطلان ما عداه من تعريفات ؛ ومذهبه المختار قد يكون تعريفا جديدًا يبتكره أو مذهبا سابقا ينتصر له . مثال ذلك : ما أورده إمام الحرمين الجويني في تعريف «البيان»، حيث أورد التعريفات السابقة، ثم كر عليها بالنقض واختار تعريفا آخر يراه أكثر صوابا، (1) المحصول في علم أصول الفقه للرازي، ج 1، ص : 78 - 80 (2) البرهان في أصول الفقه الإمام الحرمين الجويني، ج: 1، ص: 152
C. Critique of contradictory definitions: in submission to the logic of the dialectical method, the usuli is not content merely to present his definition of the term, but rather moves after that to critique the definitions of other schools and shows the points of defect in them, then refutes them with what invalidates them and leads to affirming the correctness of his own school in the definition and the falsehood of other definitions besides it. And his chosen school may be a new definition he innovates or a previous school he champions. An example of that is what Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni presented in defining 'bayan' (elucidation), where he presented previous definitions, then attacked them with critique and chose another definition he regarded as more correct.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage explains the third step in the jadal (dialectical) method when dealing with definitions: after presenting one's own definition, the scholar must critique opposing definitions. The author states that the usuli does not stop at giving his own definition; he goes on to examine the definitions of other schools, identify their flaws, and refute them. This process reinforces the correctness of his own definition and demonstrates the invalidity of alternatives. The chosen position may be an original definition or a previously held school. The author illustrates with an example: al-Juwayni's approach to defining 'bayan' (elucidation) in his work al-Burhan. By presenting existing definitions and then refuting them, al-Juwayni selects what he considers the most correct definition. This passage highlights the critical and argumentative nature of jadal in usul al-fiqh.

The Dialectical Method of Critique: Juwayni's Refutation of Definitions of al-Bayan
Author explains the jadal method and illustrates it with Juwayni's critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the steps of the dialectical method (presentation, critique, refutation, selection) as demonstrated in Juwayni's critique of definitions of al-bayan.

Core Idea
The dialectical method requires not just defining a term, but actively refuting competing definitions.

In the Islamic legal tradition, establishing a definition is not complete until contrary definitions have been examined and refuted. This passage demonstrates the jadal method through Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni's critique of earlier definitions of al-bayan (clarification). He presents two defective definitions, shows why they fail, and then endorses al-Baqillani's definition as sound. This process of naqd (refutation) is essential for ensuring that the chosen definition is rigorous.

Guided Path
1
Identify the competing definitions
Find the two definitions of al-bayan that Juwayni rejects. Note their content and the sources he attributes them to.
The first definition is 'removal from ambiguity to clarity'; the second is 'knowledge'.
2
Analyze Juwayni's objections
For each rejected definition, identify the specific defect Juwayni points out. What is his rationale for rejecting each?
First: metaphorical language unsuitable for precise definitions. Second: disconnection from actual understanding.
3
Recognize the standard for a valid definition
What criteria does Juwayni imply for an acceptable definition? Look for his description of ideal definitional expressions.
Definitions should be clear, precise, without deficiency or excess, understood by beginners and advanced.
4
Identify the chosen definition
What is al-Baqillani's definition that Juwayni endorses? How does it avoid the defects of the previous definitions?
Al-bayan is proof (dalil), divided into rational and transmitted. It ties clarification to evidence.
5
Map the dialectical structure
The author describes a three-step process: present, critique, refute, then affirm one's own doctrine. Outline these steps using Juwayni's example.
Juwayni presents (defective definitions), critiques (shows defects), refutes (invalidates them), then affirms (his own choice).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ج - نقد التعريفات المخالفة : خضوعا لمنطق المنهج الجدلي، فإن الأصولي لا يكتفي فحسب بتقديم تعريفه للمصطلح، بل ينتقل بعد ذلك إلى نقد تعريفات الاتجاهات الأخرى ويبين مواضع الخلل فيها، ثم يرد عليها بما ينقضها ويفضي إلى التأكيد على صحة مذهبه في التعريف وبطلان ما عداه من تعريفات؛ ومذهبه المختار قد يكون تعريفا جديدًا يبتكره أو مذهبا سابقا ينتصر له. مثال ذلك: ما أورده إمام الحرمين الجويني في تعريف «البيان»، حيث أورد التعريفات السابقة، ثم كر عليها بالنقض واختار تعريفا آخر يراه أكثر صوابا، وذلك إذ يقول رحمه الله: اختلفت عبارات الخائضين في هذا الفن في معنى (البيان): فذهب بعض من ينسب إلى الأصوليين إلى أن البيان إخراج الشيء من حيز الإشكال إلى حيز التجلي والوضوح. وهذه العبارة وإن كانت محومة على المقصود فليست مرضية، فإنها مشتملة على ألفاظ مستعارة كالحيز والتجلي، وذوو البصائر لا يودعون مقاصد الحدود إلا في عبارات هي قوالب تبلغ الغرض من غير قصور ولا ازدياد يفهمها المبتدئون ويحسنها المنتهون. وقال قائل: البيان هو العلم.. وهو غير مرضي، فإن الإنسان ينهي الكلام إلى حد البيان، ويحسن منه أن يقول: تم البيان وإن لم يفهم المخاطب، وقد يقول: بينت فلم يتبين. والقول المرضي في البيان؛ ما ذكره القاضي أبو بكر، حيث قال: البيان هو الدليل، ثم الدليل ينقسم إلى العقلي والسمعي والله سبحانه وتعالى مبين الأمور المعقولة بنصب الأدلة العقلية عليها، والمسمع المخاطب مبين للمخاطب ما يبغيه إذا استقل كلامه بالإبانة والإشعار بالغرض، فهذا منتهى المقصود في هذا الفن (1).
C - Critique of contrary definitions: As a submission to the logic of the dialectical method, the usuli is not content with merely presenting his definition of the term, but then moves on to critique the definitions of other trends and shows the points of defect in them, then refutes them with what invalidates them and leads to affirmation of the soundness of his own doctrine in definition and the falsity of other definitions; and his chosen doctrine may be a new definition he innovates or a previous doctrine he supports. An example of that is what Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni presented concerning the definition of 'al-bayan', where he presented the earlier definitions, then returned upon them with refutation and chose another definition he considered more correct, and that when he said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'The expressions of those who delve into this art have differed concerning the meaning of al-bayan. Some who are attributed to the usuliyyun held that al-bayan is the removal of a thing from the realm of ambiguity to the realm of clarity and obviousness. And this expression, even if it approximates the intended meaning, is not satisfactory, for it contains metaphorical words like 'realm' and 'clarity', and people of insight do not deposit the objectives of definitions except in expressions that are molds that achieve the purpose without deficiency or excess, which beginners understand and the advanced approve. Another said: al-bayan is knowledge... and it is unsatisfactory, for a person may bring speech to the point of clarification, and it may be proper for him to say 'the clarification is complete' even if the audience did not understand, and he may say 'I clarified but it did not become clear.' The satisfactory statement concerning al-bayan is what al-Qadi Abu Bakr mentioned, where he said: al-bayan is the proof (dalil), and the proof is divided into rational and transmitted, and Allah Almighty clarifies intellectual matters by setting up rational proofs over them, while the speaker who addresses clarifies to the addressee what he intends when his speech is sufficient for elucidation and indication of the purpose. This is the ultimate goal in this art.'
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage illustrates the dialectical method (al-manhaj al-jadali) in usul al-fiqh. The author explains that the usuli does not stop at defining his term; he must then critique contrary definitions, showing their defects and refuting them, thereby affirming the soundness of his own definition. The example given is Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni's treatment of the term 'al-bayan' (clarification). Juwayni first presents two defective definitions of bayan. The first defines it as 'removal from ambiguity to clarity,' but Juwayni rejects it for using metaphorical language unfit for precise definitions. The second defines bayan as 'knowledge,' but Juwayni argues that it fails because one can say 'the clarification is complete' even if the audience remains ignorant. After refuting these, Juwayni endorses al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani's definition: 'al-bayan is the proof (al-dalil).' He distinguishes between rational proofs (for intellectual matters) and transmitted proofs (for scriptural matters). This definition is deemed satisfactory because it ties bayan to evidence that actually produces understanding. The passage thus demonstrates the jadal process of naqd (refutation) and selection of a sounder definition.

Key Terms
البيان
النقد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Juwayni reject the definition of al-bayan as 'removal from the realm of ambiguity to clarity'?
A) Because it uses metaphorical language unsuitable for definitions.
B) Because it is too vague.
C) Because it does not include rational proofs.
D) Because it implies the audience understands.

Key Takeaway
The dialectical method in usul al-fiqh requires the scholar to present his definition, critique contrary definitions with precise objections, and then affirm his own definition as sound.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. Identify a definition from usul al-fiqh that has been contested (e.g., definition of qiyas or ijma). Using the dialectical method, outline what objections could be raised against it and how a defender might refute those objections. Write a brief exchange in the style of Juwayni.
?
2. In the passage, Juwayni rejects the definition of bayan as 'knowledge' because one can say 'I clarified but it did not become clear.' Analyze this objection: What logical principle does Juwayni rely on? Is his objection valid? Justify your answer.

The Role of Proof in Usuli Dialectic
Author explains why evidence is essential for compelling conviction in usuli dialectic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why evidence (hujja) is essential for persuasion in usuli dialectic and identify the two functions evidence serves in debate.

Core Idea
Persuasion in usuli dialectic requires a proof that blocks all escape routes for the opponent.

This passage grounds usuli dialectic in rigorous argumentation. The author stresses that dialectic is not mere debate but a structured exchange where evidence compels acceptance. He defines hujja as a mental movement, emphasizing its rational force over verbal artistry. Understanding this principle is essential for any scholar engaging in munazara.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of dialectic
The author states that the purpose of dialogue is persuasion (iqna'), not just exchange.
This distinguishes dialectic from sophistry.
2
Locate the definition of hujja (proof)
Hujja is a mental movement (haraka 'aqliyya) before being a verbal structure. It has a specific arrangement of elements and relations.
This emphasizes the logical structure over rhetoric.
3
Explain how persuasion is achieved
Persuasion forces the listener to accept by blocking all avenues of escape. The listener, if unwilling, will exploit any loophole.
This is the compulsive nature of proof.
4
State the two roles of evidence
Evidence must both prove the claim and refute any doubts (shubah) arising about the subject or the evidence itself.
This shows the dual function of proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الثاني: أهمية الاستدلال في الجدل الأصولي ينطوي الاستدلال في الجدل الأصولي على أهمية بالغة، ذلك أن الجدل حوار وما دام الغرض من الحوار إنما هو الإقناع فإن الإقناع لا يمكن أن يحصل إلا بالحجة التي هي حركة عقلية قبل أن تكون بنية لفظية مؤلفة من عناصر معينة تربط بينها علاقات معينة وتترتب فيما بينها ترتيبا معينا . إن الإقناع يكون بإلزام المستمع بقبول الرأي عندما يضطر إلى ذلك اضطرارا، وعندما يجد جميع منافذ الإفلات من التسليم مسدودة، ولهذا ينبغي للمستدل أن يبادر إلى سد هذه المنافذ التي يمكن أن يفلت منها المستمع الذي لا يمكن أن يمنعه أي مانع من استعمالها إن كان رافضا لرأي المتحدث . وهكذا فإن الجدال لا يكون مفيدا وموضوعيا إلا إذا توفرت الأدلة على إثباته، ودحض ما يمكن أن ينشأ حول الموضوع وحول الأدلة المثبتة من شبه .
The second topic: The importance of reasoning in usuli dialectic. Reasoning in usuli dialectic carries great importance, because dialectic is a dialogue, and as long as the purpose of dialogue is persuasion, persuasion cannot be achieved except through a proof (hujja), which is a mental movement before being a verbal structure composed of specific elements connected by specific relations and arranged in a specific order. Persuasion is achieved by compelling the listener to accept the opinion when he is forced to do so, and when he finds all avenues of escape from submission blocked. For this reason, the one reasoning should hasten to block these avenues by which the listener might escape, and no barrier can prevent him from using them if he rejects the speaker's opinion. Thus, debate is not beneficial and objective unless evidence is available to prove it and to refute any doubts that may arise concerning the subject and the supporting evidence.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This short section emphasizes the crucial role of evidence in usuli dialectic. The author defines dialectic as a dialogue aimed at persuasion, noting that persuasion requires a proof (hujja) that is fundamentally a mental process, not merely a verbal formulation. The proof must be structured with specific elements and relations arranged in a particular order to force the listener's acceptance by blocking all possible escape routes. The listener, if unwilling to accept, will exploit any loophole; therefore, the reasoner must anticipate and seal these avenues. The passage concludes that debate is only beneficial and objective when evidence is present both to establish the claim and to refute any counter-doubts. This serves as a methodological foundation for usuli dialectic, grounding it in rigorous argumentation rather than mere rhetorical exchange.

Epistemic Hierarchy of Revealed Sources in Jadal
Author explains the epistemic hierarchy of kitab, sunna, ijma, and khabar in jadal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the epistemic hierarchy of revealed sources (Kitab, Sunna, Ijma', Khabar) back to the Qur'an and explain why Ijma' is not an independent proof.

Core Idea
All revealed knowledge ultimately traces back to the Qur'an; Ijma' and Qiyas are derivative, not primary.

In jadal (dialectical theology), understanding the relative authority of revealed sources is crucial for constructing valid arguments. This passage from a jadal treatise on usul al-fiqh clarifies the hierarchy: the Qur'an is the foundation, the Sunna derives from it, and consensus (Ijma') and solitary reports (Khabar al-Wahid) depend on a chain of transmission that goes back to the Qur'an. Let's unpack this epistemic chain step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ultimate origin of sam'iyyat
The author states that in the ranks of transmitted matters (al-sam'iyyat), the Book (Kitab) is the origin. Everything else is either a transmission of it or reliant upon it. Note that the author explicitly says: 'the origin of transmitted matters is the speech of God Almighty.'
2
Trace the derivation of Sunna and Ijma'
The Sunna is received from the Book, meaning it is not an independent source but explains and supplements the Qur'an. As for Ijma', the author argues it is not on the rank of apparent meanings (zawahir) and certainly not a text. Instead, Ijma' is based on a report (khabar) that is certain (mutawatir). The custom of scholars indicates that their agreement relies on such a report.
The author uses the example of verse 4:115 to show that Ijma' is often tied to a textual basis.
3
Understand the chain of reliance from Ijma' to the Qur'an
The report underlying Ijma' is accepted because God commands its acceptance. God's command is from His speech, which is received from the Messenger, and the Messenger's truthfulness is proven by miracles. Thus, Ijma' is not a proof in itself but is derived from a mutawatir report that ultimately originates from the Qur'an.
This refutes the misconception that Ijma' is an independent source equal to the Qur'an.
4
Distinguish mutawatir and solitary reports
The author specifies that the report in question is al-khabar al-mutawatir, which yields certain knowledge. The solitary report (khabar al-wahid) is not independent; it relies on mutawatir reports or on Ijma' that itself rests on mutawatir. Similarly, analogy (qiyas) is not an independent source but is based on the same chain.
This hierarchy ensures that all valid evidence in jadal traces back to the Qur'an with certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوب اتصاف العالم بالشيء بالنطق الحق الصدق عما هو عالم به، فإذا ذكرنا في مراتب السمعيات الكتاب فهو الأصل، وإذا ذكرنا السنة فمنها تلقي الكتاب، والأصل الكتاب . فأما الإجماع فقد أسنده معظم العلماء إلى نص الكتاب، وذكروا قول الله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يُشَاقِقِ الرَّسُولَ مِنْ بَعْدِ مَا نَبَيَّنَ لَهُ الْهُدَى وَيَتَّبِعْ غَيْرَ سَبِيلِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ (1) ، وهذا عندنا ليس على رتبة الظواهر، فضلا عن ادعاء منصب النص فيها، وإنما يتلقى الإجماع من أمر متعلق بالعادة أولا، فإن علماء الدهر إذا قطعوا أقوالهم جزمًا في مظنون وعلم استحالة التواطؤ منهم، فالعرف يقضي باستناد اعتقادهم واتفاقهم إلى خبر مقطوع به عندهم ... فإذا ليس الإجماع في نفسه دليلا بل العرف قاض باستناده إلى خبر والخبر مقبول من أمر الله تعالى بقبوله، وأمر الله من كلامه، وكلامه متلقى من رسوله، وصدق رسوله من مدلول تصديق الله تعالى إياه بالمعجزة، وما ذكرناه من الخبر في أثناء الكلام ؛ عنينا به الخبر المتواتر النص الذي ثبت أصله وفحواه قطعا . فأما خبر الواحد، إن عد من مراتب السمعيات فلا نعني بذكره أنه يستقل بنفسه، ولكن العمل عنده يستند إلى خبر متواتر، وإلى إجماع مستند إلى الخبر المتواتر، وكذلك القول في القياس . وبالجملة : أصل السمعيات كلام الله تعالى وما عداه طريق نقله أو مستند إليه»
The necessity of the scholar's description of a thing by true speech about what he knows: if we mention the ranks of the transmitted matters, the Book is the origin; if we mention the Sunna, from it the Book is received, and the origin is the Book. As for consensus, most scholars have ascribed it to the text of the Book, and they mentioned the saying of God Almighty: 'And whoever opposes the Messenger after guidance has become clear to him and follows other than the way of the believers' (4:115). This, in our view, is not on the rank of apparent meanings, let alone claiming the status of text in them. Rather, consensus is initially received from a matter related to custom: if the scholars of the age decisively cut off their statements in a probable matter, and it is known that collusion among them is impossible, then custom judges that their belief and agreement is based on a certain report they possess... Thus consensus is not in itself a proof, but custom judges that it is based on a report, and the report is accepted by the command of God Almighty to accept it, and the command of God is from His speech, and His speech is received from His Messenger, and the truthfulness of His Messenger is from the implication of God Almighty's verification of him by miracles. What we mentioned of the report in the course of speech—we meant by it the mutawatir report that is text, whose origin and content are established conclusively. As for the solitary report, if it is counted among the ranks of transmitted matters, we do not mean by mentioning it that it is independent by itself, but action based on it is reliant on a mutawatir report, and on consensus reliant on the mutawatir report. The same is said about analogy. In summary: the origin of transmitted matters is the speech of God Almighty, and everything else is a means of its transmission or a reliance on it.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological exposition on the hierarchy of sources in Islamic jurisprudence as discussed in jadal (dialectical theology). The author begins by asserting that knowledge of a thing must be based on truthful speech. Within the ranks of sam'iyyat (revealed matters), the Qur'an (Kitab) is the origin; the Sunna is derived from it. Consensus (ijma') is not an independent proof but relies on a report (khabar) that is certain, specifically a mutawatir report. The author argues that ijma' itself is not a primary source; rather, the custom among scholars indicates that their agreement is based on a strong report. That report is accepted because God commands its acceptance, and God's command is known through His speech, which comes via the Messenger. The Messenger's truthfulness is proven by miracles. The report referred to here is the mutawatir report, which is definitive. The solitary report (khabar al-wahid), if considered among the transmitted matters, does not stand alone but depends on mutawatir reports or consensus that itself rests on mutawatir reports. The same applies to qiyas (analogy). The key point is that all revealed knowledge ultimately traces back to the Qur'an; any other source is either a means of transmitting it or derived from it. This passage guards against the misconception that ijma' or qiyas are independent sources equal to the Qur'an and Sunna.

Key Terms
السمعيات
الخبر المتواتر
الإجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) The Sunna
D) Analogical reasoning (Qiyas)

Key Takeaway
The origin of all sam'iyyat is the speech of God (Qur'an); other sources like Ijma' and Qiyas are derivative and depend on a chain that traces back to the Qur'an.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Qur'anic Proof That a Command Implies Obligation
Author gives first example of usuli inference from Qur'an

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the usuli inference from Qur'an 24:63 that al-amr (command) indicates obligation in the absence of a contextual indicator.

Core Idea
The threat of punishment proves that disobeying a command is abandoning an obligation.

The usuliyyun ground their rule that a command implies obligation in the Qur'an itself. In this lesson, we examine their inference from the threat of punishment in verse 24:63. The logic is that a threat of punishment is only attached to abandoning an obligation, so the command must be obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the verse and the claim
The usuliyyun cite Qur'an 24:63: 'Let those beware who contradict the Prophet's command, lest a trial befall them or a painful torment.' They claim this verse shows that a command implies obligation.
2
Extract the logical structure
The reasoning: God threatens punishment for contradicting the Prophet's command. Punishment is only threatened for abandoning an obligatory act (wajib). Therefore, obeying the command is obligatory.
This is a syllogistic inference.
3
Check the underlying assumptions
The major premise is that God's threat of punishment is always attached to the abandonment of an obligation. This is derived from the general principle that God does not punish for non-obligatory matters.
The usuliyyun assume this premise is known from the Shari'a.
4
Apply to the rule of al-amr
Thus, a command (amr) indicates obligation unless there is a contextual indicator (qarīna) suggesting otherwise. The verse provides scriptural evidence for this usul rule.
This rule is foundational in fiqh for deriving obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما مألوف العرب في الخطاب، فقد دعا الأصوليين إلى الاهتمام به نزول النص القرآني، وكذا ورود السنة النبوية على وفق هذا المألوف، وطبقا لقواعده ومبادئه، بحيث لا يمكن فهم نصوص الوحي إلا في إطار قواعد اللغة العربية ومألوف العرب في الخطاب. ولذلك فإن الأصوليين لم يكتفوا باستنباط القواعد اللغوية وتقريرها لتفسير النصوص، بل راحوا يستقرئون الأدلة من واقع مألوف العرب في الخطاب لإسناد هذه القواعد وإثباتها . وفيما يلي نماذج من استدلالات (1) الأصوليين بالأدلة النقلية : أ - استدلال الأصوليين بالكتاب على القواعد الأصولية : من ذلك ؛ استدلالهم على اقتضاء الأمر المجرد عن القرينة الإيجاب، بقوله تعالى : هو ... فَلْيَحْذَرِ الَّذِينَ يُخَالِفُونَ عَنْ أَمْرِهِ أَن تُصِيبَهُمْ فِتْنَةٌ أَوْ يُصِيبَهُمْ عَذَابٌ اليو (2) ، فإن الله قد توعد الذين يخالفون أمر الرسول لا بأن تصيبهم فتنة أو صلى الله عليه وسلم يصيبهم عذاب أليم، ولا يتوعد بالفتنة والعذاب إلا على ترك الواجب، فثبت أن امتثال أمره واجب ذلك أيضا ؛ استدلالهم على عدم جواز التكليف بما لا يطاق شرعًا بقوله تعالى : لا يُكَلِّفُ اللهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا .. ، ووجه الاستدلال أن الله نفى من شرعه تكليف النفس بما لا تستطيع، فإن الوسع في اللغة هو الطاقة والجهد (5) ومن ذلك كذلك ؛ استدلالهم بمجموع آيتين فأكثر في موضع واحد، بحيث لا تستقل إحدى الآيتين بالدلالة على القاعدة حتى تضم إليه الآية أو الآيات الأخرى، وذلك كما في استدلالهم على أنه ليس من شروط الاستثناء كون المستثنى أقل من المستثنى منه بقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ عِبَادِى لَيْسَ لَكَ عَلَيْهِمْ سُلْطَانُ إِلَّا
As for the customary usage of the Arabs in discourse, it prompted the legal theorists to pay attention to the fact that the Qur'anic text was revealed, and likewise the Prophetic Sunna came, in accordance with this customary usage and its rules and principles, such that the texts of revelation cannot be understood except within the framework of the rules of the Arabic language and the customary usage of the Arabs in discourse. Therefore, the legal theorists did not content themselves with deriving and establishing linguistic rules to interpret texts, but rather they inferred evidence from the reality of Arab customary usage to support and prove these rules. Below are examples of the legal theorists' inferences using transmitted evidence: A. The legal theorists' inference from the Book regarding fundamental legal rules: from that is their inference that a command devoid of context indicates obligation, by His saying: '...So let those beware who contradict the Prophet's command, lest a trial befall them or a painful torment.' (24:63) For God has threatened those who contradict the command of the Messenger with a trial or a painful torment, and He does not threaten with trial and torment except for abandoning an obligation, so it is established that obeying His command is obligatory. Also, their inference regarding the impermissibility of legally charging someone with what is beyond their capacity, by His saying: 'God does not charge a soul except with what is within its capacity' (2:286). The aspect of inference is that God negated in His law charging a soul with what it cannot do, for 'capacity' in language is ability and strength. Also from that is their inference from two or more verses in one place, such that one of the two verses does not independently indicate the rule until the other verse(s) are added to it, as in their inference that it is not a condition of exception that the excepted item be less than the excepted-from item, by His saying: 'Indeed, My servants — you have no authority over them, except...' (15:42) etc.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage presents examples of how usuliyyun (legal theorists) use the Qur'an to establish principles of usul al-fiqh. The author first explains that the Qur'an and Sunna were revealed in line with Arab customary discourse, so understanding revelation requires knowledge of Arabic language rules. The usuliyyun not only derive linguistic rules from texts but also infer evidence from actual Arab usage. Then two main examples are given from the Qur'an: (1) The verse 'Let those beware who contradict the Prophet's command...' is used to prove that a command implies obligation. The reasoning: God threatens punishment for disobeying the Prophet's command; such a threat is only for abandoning an obligation, so obeying the command is wajib. (2) The verse 'God does not charge a soul except with what is within its capacity' is used to prove that legal obligation does not exceed capacity. The word 'capacity' (wus') means ability/effort. Additionally, the passage mentions a third example involving two verses together to show that exception does not require the excepted item to be less than the excepted-from item, citing 'Except My servants among them...' (15:42). These examples demonstrate the method of istidlal (inference) from the Qur'an to support usul al-fiqh rules. The passage guards against the misconception that usul al-fiqh rules are merely speculative; they are grounded in scriptural evidence.

الوُجوب
القرينة
فَلْيَحْذَرِ الَّذِينَ يُخَالِفُونَ عَنْ أَمْرِهِ

The threat of punishment in the Qur'an is the scriptural basis for the usuli principle that a command implies obligation unless a contextual indicator suggests otherwise.
